Perseverance in Dhikr Despite Heedlessness
Sanusi defines two types of dhikr and explains the stages of verbal remembrance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a beginner should never abandon dhikr due to heedlessness and how dhikr can elevate one through three stages: heedlessness, presence, and absence.

Core Idea
Even heedless dhikr can elevate you to higher states.

Sanusi begins by categorizing dhikr into two types, then immediately addresses a common pitfall: the beginner's tendency to stop dhikr when feeling distracted. He reassures us that even imperfect remembrance is valuable and can lead to profound spiritual states. This lesson unpacks that principle and the progressive stages of verbal dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two types and the principle
Read the Arabic and translation from 'والذكر نوعان' down to 'وما ذلك على الله بعزيز'. Notice the definition and the core instruction: do not abandon dhikr due to heedlessness.
The quote from Ibn Ata'illah reinforces the point.
2
Identify the three stages of dhikr
Find the progression: dhikr with heedlessness, with presence, with absence from other than the Remembered. Understand how each leads to the next.
3
Reflect on the heart becoming the house of the Lord
The passage says when one reaches absence, the heart becomes the house of God and dhikr arises spontaneously. Consider what this means spiritually.
This is a high station.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان نوعي الذكر
والذكر نوعان:
الأول : الذِّكرُ باللسان، وهو شأن أصحاب البدايات، فيجب عليهم موالاة الذكر باللسان مع تكلُّف الحضور بالقلب، حتّى يصير الحضور طبيعة له .
ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه، فلَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع غفلة يرفعه إلى الذِّكر مع الحضور، ولَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع حضور، يرفعه إلى الذكر مع الغيبة عما سوى المذكور، فإذا غاب عما سوى المذكور استغرق في عين بحر الوحدة، فيصير القلب حينئذ بيتَ الرَّبِّ ،تعالى، فينشأ الذكر من غير قصد ولا تدبر لامتزاجه بروحه وجسمه .

قوله: (ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه . . . إلخ) : في كلامه إشارة لقول صاحب الحكم»: لا تترك الذكر لعدم حضورك مع الله تعالى فيه؛ لأنَّ غفلتك عن وجود ذكره أشدُّ من غفلتك مع وجود ذكره، وعسى أن يرفعك من ذكر مع وجود غفلة إلى ذكر مع وجود يقظة، ومن ذكر مع وجود يقظة إلى ذكر مع وجود حضور، ومن ذكر مع وجود حضور إلى ذكر مع وجود غيبة عما سوى المذكور، وما ذلك على الله بعزيز) (۱)

وأنواع الذكر اللساني كثيرة؛ منها : التَّسبيحُ والتَّكبير وتلاوة القرآن وغير ذلك، وأسرعُها إجابة للمبتدئ (لا إله إلّا الله) مفردة عن (محمد رسول الله) على التحقيق فيما عدا الختم فإذا أراد الختم ختم بها، وفي بعض الطُّرُقِ الشَّاذليَّة أنَّه يذكرها على رأس كل مئة ، هذا إذا ذكر وحده، أما إذا ذكر مع جماعة ؛ فلا يذكرها إلا عند الختم مع إخوانه، ولهذا درج أرباب الطُّرُق المحمَّديَّة على الاقتصار عليها، فإذا كمل السَّالك فالأفضل له أن يضمّ معها (محمد رسول الله)، والأفضل حينئذ الاشتغال بتلاوة القرآن ليتخلق به وتُفاض عليه العلوم اللدنية من أسراره، فإن لم يكن يحفظ القرآن اشتغل بسماعه ممن يقرؤه وإن كان القارئ صاحب غفلة، ويكون الأمر على حد قول العارف بالله تعالى سيدي عمر ابن الفارض الله [ من الكامل] (1).
Statement of the two types of dhikr.
And dhikr is two types:
The first: dhikr with the tongue, and it is the concern of the people of beginnings. So it is obligatory upon them to persevere in dhikr with the tongue while striving for presence (ḥuḍūr) in the heart, until presence becomes natural for them.
And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness (ghafla) in it. For perhaps a dhikr with heedlessness elevates him to dhikr with presence, and perhaps a dhikr with presence elevates him to dhikr with absence (ghayba) from other than the Remembered. So when he becomes absent from other than the Remembered, he becomes immersed in the very ocean of Oneness (waḥda). Then the heart at that moment becomes the house of the Lord, exalted, and dhikr arises from him without intention or deliberation due to its mingling with his spirit and body.

His saying: (And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness in it... etc.) In his speech is an allusion to the saying of the author of al-Ḥikam: 'Do not abandon dhikr due to your lack of presence with God Almighty in it; for your heedlessness of the existence of your dhikr is more severe than your heedlessness with the existence of your dhikr. And perhaps He will raise you from dhikr with heedlessness to dhikr with vigilance, and from dhikr with vigilance to dhikr with presence, and from dhikr with presence to dhikr with absence from other than the Remembered. And that is not difficult for God.' (1)

And the types of verbal dhikr are many; among them: glorification (tasbīḥ), magnification (takbīr), recitation of the Qur'an, and other than that. And the swiftest of them in response for the beginner is 'there is no god but God' (lā ilāha illā Allāh) separate from 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God' (Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh) according to verification, except for the conclusion (khatm). So if he intends the conclusion, he concludes with it. And in some of the Shādhilī ways, he mentions it at the head of every hundred. This is when he makes dhikr alone. But when he makes dhikr with a group, he only mentions it at the conclusion with his brethren. Hence the masters of the Muḥammadan ways proceeded to restrict themselves to it. So when the wayfarer (sālik) becomes complete, it is best for him to combine with it 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God'. And the best then is to occupy himself with recitation of the Qur'an to be characterized by it and for the esoteric sciences (al-ʿulūm al-laduniyya) to be poured upon him from its secrets. And if he does not memorize the Qur'an, he should occupy himself with listening to it from whoever recites it, even if the reciter is heedless. And the matter is like the saying of the knower of God, my master ʿUmar ibn al-Fāriḍ, may God [bless him]? (1).
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the two types of dhikr (remembrance of God), with a detailed focus on the first type: verbal dhikr (dhikr bil-lisān). The author begins by stating that dhikr is of two types, then immediately describes the first type: verbal dhikr, which is the concern of beginners. He explains that such individuals must persevere in verbal dhikr while exerting themselves to attain heart presence (ḥuḍūr), until it becomes natural. A key principle is that one should not abandon dhikr due to the presence of heedlessness (ghafla). The author then outlines a three-stage progression: (1) dhikr with heedlessness may lead to, (2) dhikr with presence, which in turn may lead to (3) dhikr with absence (ghayba) from everything other than the Remembered. When one reaches this stage, he becomes immersed in the ocean of Divine Oneness (waḥda), and the heart becomes the house of God, such that dhikr flows spontaneously without intention or deliberation because it is mingled with his entire being. The author then cites a quotation from Ibn ʿAṭāʾillāh (author of al-Ḥikam) to reinforce this teaching, emphasizing that heedlessness of the act of dhikr itself is worse than heedlessness during dhikr, and that God can elevate one through successive stages. Next, the author lists the many types of verbal dhikr, including tasbīḥ (glorification), takbīr (magnification), and tilāwah (recitation) of the Qurʾān. He notes that the most swiftly answered for the beginner is the phrase 'lā ilāha illā Allāh' without the addition of 'Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh', except at the conclusion (khatm) of a dhikr session. He describes specific practices of the Shādhilī order and other Muhammadan orders, where the phrase is repeated either alone or with the group, and the practice of concluding with it. For the advanced wayfarer (sālik), it is better to add 'Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh' and to occupy oneself with recitation of the Qurʾān to acquire its character and receive divine sciences (ʿulūm laduniyya). If one does not know the Qurʾān by heart, listening to its recitation is beneficial even from a heedless reciter. The passage concludes with a reference to the poet ʿUmar ibn al-Fāriḍ.

Key Terms
ذكر
لسان
قلب
حضور
غفلة
غيبة
وحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If I feel heedless during dhikr, it is invalid and I should stop.
Correction: The author explicitly says do not abandon dhikr due to heedlessness; even heedless dhikr is beneficial and can lead to presence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why should a beginner not abandon dhikr when heedless?
A) Because heedless dhikr is better than no dhikr and may lead to presence.
B) Because heedless dhikr is still accepted by God.
C) Because the heart is always present even if the mind wanders.
D) Because dhikr must be done continuously regardless of state.

Key Takeaway
Perseverance in dhikr, even when heedless, is a powerful means of spiritual ascent through stages of presence and absence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your mind wanders during dhikr, do you feel like giving up or that your effort is wasted? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what concrete change will you make in your daily dhikr habit starting today?
?
Are there moments in your life where you abandon a good deed because you cannot do it perfectly? Where else might this hidden perfectionism be holding you back from spiritual growth?
?
Imagine your heart truly becoming the 'house of the Lord.' What would change about your priorities, fears, and desires? What is one step you can take this week to move from heedless dhikr toward more present dhikr?

The Best Phrase for Beginners: La Ilaha Illa Allah
Sanusi enumerates types of verbal dhikr and gives practical rules for beginners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the many types of verbal dhikr, understand why 'la ilaha illa Allah' is most effective for beginners, and learn the proper way to conclude a dhikr session.

Core Idea
The simplest phrase is often the most powerful for beginners.

After establishing the importance of verbal dhikr, Sanusi now categorizes its many forms. He highlights which phrase is most responsive for the beginner and provides guidance on its use, especially concerning the conclusion (khatm) of a dhikr session. This lesson also touches on group dhikr practices in the Shadhili and Muhammadi orders.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of verbal dhikr types and the recommended phrase
Read from 'وأنواع الذكر اللساني كثيرة' down to 'إلا عند الختم مع إخوانه'. Note the variety and the special mention of la ilaha illa Allah.
The author says it is 'the swiftest in response for the beginner'.
2
Understand the exception for the conclusion (khatm)
The phrase is used separately except at the end of a session, where it is repeated. Also in some Shadhili ways it is said every hundred.
3
Review group dhikr practice
When in a group, the phrase is only uttered at the conclusion. This was the practice of the Muhammadi wayfarers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان نوعي الذكر
والذكر نوعان:
الأول : الذِّكرُ باللسان، وهو شأن أصحاب البدايات، فيجب عليهم موالاة الذكر باللسان مع تكلُّف الحضور بالقلب، حتّى يصير الحضور طبيعة له .
ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه، فلَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع غفلة يرفعه إلى الذِّكر مع الحضور، ولَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع حضور، يرفعه إلى الذكر مع الغيبة عما سوى المذكور، فإذا غاب عما سوى المذكور استغرق في عين بحر الوحدة، فيصير القلب حينئذ بيتَ الرَّبِّ ،تعالى، فينشأ الذكر من غير قصد ولا تدبر لامتزاجه بروحه وجسمه .

قوله: (ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه . . . إلخ) : في كلامه إشارة لقول صاحب الحكم»: لا تترك الذكر لعدم حضورك مع الله تعالى فيه؛ لأنَّ غفلتك عن وجود ذكره أشدُّ من غفلتك مع وجود ذكره، وعسى أن يرفعك من ذكر مع وجود غفلة إلى ذكر مع وجود يقظة، ومن ذكر مع وجود يقظة إلى ذكر مع وجود حضور، ومن ذكر مع وجود حضور إلى ذكر مع وجود غيبة عما سوى المذكور، وما ذلك على الله بعزيز) (۱)

وأنواع الذكر اللساني كثيرة؛ منها : التَّسبيحُ والتَّكبير وتلاوة القرآن وغير ذلك، وأسرعُها إجابة للمبتدئ (لا إله إلّا الله) مفردة عن (محمد رسول الله) على التحقيق فيما عدا الختم فإذا أراد الختم ختم بها، وفي بعض الطُّرُقِ الشَّاذليَّة أنَّه يذكرها على رأس كل مئة ، هذا إذا ذكر وحده، أما إذا ذكر مع جماعة ؛ فلا يذكرها إلا عند الختم مع إخوانه، ولهذا درج أرباب الطُّرُق المحمَّديَّة على الاقتصار عليها، فإذا كمل السَّالك فالأفضل له أن يضمّ معها (محمد رسول الله)، والأفضل حينئذ الاشتغال بتلاوة القرآن ليتخلق به وتُفاض عليه العلوم اللدنية من أسراره، فإن لم يكن يحفظ القرآن اشتغل بسماعه ممن يقرؤه وإن كان القارئ صاحب غفلة، ويكون الأمر على حد قول العارف بالله تعالى سيدي عمر ابن الفارض الله [ من الكامل] (1).
Statement of the two types of dhikr.
And dhikr is two types:
The first: dhikr with the tongue, and it is the concern of the people of beginnings. So it is obligatory upon them to persevere in dhikr with the tongue while striving for presence (ḥuḍūr) in the heart, until presence becomes natural for them.
And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness (ghafla) in it. For perhaps a dhikr with heedlessness elevates him to dhikr with presence, and perhaps a dhikr with presence elevates him to dhikr with absence (ghayba) from other than the Remembered. So when he becomes absent from other than the Remembered, he becomes immersed in the very ocean of Oneness (waḥda). Then the heart at that moment becomes the house of the Lord, exalted, and dhikr arises from him without intention or deliberation due to its mingling with his spirit and body.

His saying: (And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness in it... etc.) In his speech is an allusion to the saying of the author of al-Ḥikam: 'Do not abandon dhikr due to your lack of presence with God Almighty in it; for your heedlessness of the existence of your dhikr is more severe than your heedlessness with the existence of your dhikr. And perhaps He will raise you from dhikr with heedlessness to dhikr with vigilance, and from dhikr with vigilance to dhikr with presence, and from dhikr with presence to dhikr with absence from other than the Remembered. And that is not difficult for God.' (1)

And the types of verbal dhikr are many; among them: glorification (tasbīḥ), magnification (takbīr), recitation of the Qur'an, and other than that. And the swiftest of them in response for the beginner is 'there is no god but God' (lā ilāha illā Allāh) separate from 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God' (Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh) according to verification, except for the conclusion (khatm). So if he intends the conclusion, he concludes with it. And in some of the Shādhilī ways, he mentions it at the head of every hundred. This is when he makes dhikr alone. But when he makes dhikr with a group, he only mentions it at the conclusion with his brethren. Hence the masters of the Muḥammadan ways proceeded to restrict themselves to it. So when the wayfarer (sālik) becomes complete, it is best for him to combine with it 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God'. And the best then is to occupy himself with recitation of the Qur'an to be characterized by it and for the esoteric sciences (al-ʿulūm al-laduniyya) to be poured upon him from its secrets. And if he does not memorize the Qur'an, he should occupy himself with listening to it from whoever recites it, even if the reciter is heedless. And the matter is like the saying of the knower of God, my master ʿUmar ibn al-Fāriḍ, may God [bless him]? (1).
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the two types of dhikr (remembrance of God), with a detailed focus on the first type: verbal dhikr (dhikr bil-lisān). The author begins by stating that dhikr is of two types, then immediately describes the first type: verbal dhikr, which is the concern of beginners. He explains that such individuals must persevere in verbal dhikr while exerting themselves to attain heart presence (ḥuḍūr), until it becomes natural. A key principle is that one should not abandon dhikr due to the presence of heedlessness (ghafla). The author then outlines a three-stage progression: (1) dhikr with heedlessness may lead to, (2) dhikr with presence, which in turn may lead to (3) dhikr with absence (ghayba) from everything other than the Remembered. When one reaches this stage, he becomes immersed in the ocean of Divine Oneness (waḥda), and the heart becomes the house of God, such that dhikr flows spontaneously without intention or deliberation because it is mingled with his entire being. The author then cites a quotation from Ibn ʿAṭāʾillāh (author of al-Ḥikam) to reinforce this teaching, emphasizing that heedlessness of the act of dhikr itself is worse than heedlessness during dhikr, and that God can elevate one through successive stages. Next, the author lists the many types of verbal dhikr, including tasbīḥ (glorification), takbīr (magnification), and tilāwah (recitation) of the Qurʾān. He notes that the most swiftly answered for the beginner is the phrase 'lā ilāha illā Allāh' without the addition of 'Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh', except at the conclusion (khatm) of a dhikr session. He describes specific practices of the Shādhilī order and other Muhammadan orders, where the phrase is repeated either alone or with the group, and the practice of concluding with it. For the advanced wayfarer (sālik), it is better to add 'Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh' and to occupy oneself with recitation of the Qurʾān to acquire its character and receive divine sciences (ʿulūm laduniyya). If one does not know the Qurʾān by heart, listening to its recitation is beneficial even from a heedless reciter. The passage concludes with a reference to the poet ʿUmar ibn al-Fāriḍ.

Misconception: For a beginner, a longer or more complex dhikr is more powerful.
Correction: The author states that the simplest phrase, la ilaha illa Allah alone, is the swiftest in response for the beginner.

Checkpoint

C) Only at the conclusion.
D) Never, the full shahada should always be recited.

Key Takeaway
For beginners, the most effective verbal dhikr is 'la ilaha illa Allah' recited alone, with specific rules for conclusion and group practice.

Advanced Remembrance: Qur'an Recitation and Spiritual Sciences
Sanusi prescribes Qur'an recitation as the best practice for advanced seekers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that for the advanced wayfarer, reciting or listening to the Qur'an is superior to other forms of dhikr, and that even listening to a heedful reciter is beneficial.

Core Idea
For the complete seeker, the Qur'an is the highest remembrance.

Sanusi now addresses the advanced seeker who has completed the basic stages. He advises that after mastering the phrase 'la ilaha illa Allah', the best occupation is the recitation of the Qur'an, which brings about divine sciences and spiritual character. He even encourages listening to the Qur'an from a reluctant reciter, citing the great saint Umar ibn al-Farid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on advanced dhikr and Qur'an recitation
Read from 'والأفضل حينئذ الاشتغال بتلاوة القرآن' to the end. Note the order: first combine the two parts, then occupy with Qur'an.
2
Understand the benefits of Qur'an recitation
It causes the seeker to be characterized by the Quran's qualities and divine sciences are poured upon him.
3
Consider the alternative of listening
If one cannot recite, listening to a reciter—even a heedless one—is still beneficial. This shows the power of the Quran itself.
Reference to Ibn al-Farid indicates the high regard for this practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان نوعي الذكر
والذكر نوعان:
الأول : الذِّكرُ باللسان، وهو شأن أصحاب البدايات، فيجب عليهم موالاة الذكر باللسان مع تكلُّف الحضور بالقلب، حتّى يصير الحضور طبيعة له .
ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه، فلَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع غفلة يرفعه إلى الذِّكر مع الحضور، ولَرُبَّ ذِكْر مع حضور، يرفعه إلى الذكر مع الغيبة عما سوى المذكور، فإذا غاب عما سوى المذكور استغرق في عين بحر الوحدة، فيصير القلب حينئذ بيتَ الرَّبِّ ،تعالى، فينشأ الذكر من غير قصد ولا تدبر لامتزاجه بروحه وجسمه .

قوله: (ولا يترك الذكر لوجود الغفلة فيه . . . إلخ) : في كلامه إشارة لقول صاحب الحكم»: لا تترك الذكر لعدم حضورك مع الله تعالى فيه؛ لأنَّ غفلتك عن وجود ذكره أشدُّ من غفلتك مع وجود ذكره، وعسى أن يرفعك من ذكر مع وجود غفلة إلى ذكر مع وجود يقظة، ومن ذكر مع وجود يقظة إلى ذكر مع وجود حضور، ومن ذكر مع وجود حضور إلى ذكر مع وجود غيبة عما سوى المذكور، وما ذلك على الله بعزيز) (۱)

وأنواع الذكر اللساني كثيرة؛ منها : التَّسبيحُ والتَّكبير وتلاوة القرآن وغير ذلك، وأسرعُها إجابة للمبتدئ (لا إله إلّا الله) مفردة عن (محمد رسول الله) على التحقيق فيما عدا الختم فإذا أراد الختم ختم بها، وفي بعض الطُّرُقِ الشَّاذليَّة أنَّه يذكرها على رأس كل مئة ، هذا إذا ذكر وحده، أما إذا ذكر مع جماعة ؛ فلا يذكرها إلا عند الختم مع إخوانه، ولهذا درج أرباب الطُّرُق المحمَّديَّة على الاقتصار عليها، فإذا كمل السَّالك فالأفضل له أن يضمّ معها (محمد رسول الله)، والأفضل حينئذ الاشتغال بتلاوة القرآن ليتخلق به وتُفاض عليه العلوم اللدنية من أسراره، فإن لم يكن يحفظ القرآن اشتغل بسماعه ممن يقرؤه وإن كان القارئ صاحب غفلة، ويكون الأمر على حد قول العارف بالله تعالى سيدي عمر ابن الفارض الله [ من الكامل] (1).
Statement of the two types of dhikr.
And dhikr is two types:
The first: dhikr with the tongue, and it is the concern of the people of beginnings. So it is obligatory upon them to persevere in dhikr with the tongue while striving for presence (ḥuḍūr) in the heart, until presence becomes natural for them.
And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness (ghafla) in it. For perhaps a dhikr with heedlessness elevates him to dhikr with presence, and perhaps a dhikr with presence elevates him to dhikr with absence (ghayba) from other than the Remembered. So when he becomes absent from other than the Remembered, he becomes immersed in the very ocean of Oneness (waḥda). Then the heart at that moment becomes the house of the Lord, exalted, and dhikr arises from him without intention or deliberation due to its mingling with his spirit and body.

His saying: (And one should not abandon dhikr due to the existence of heedlessness in it... etc.) In his speech is an allusion to the saying of the author of al-Ḥikam: 'Do not abandon dhikr due to your lack of presence with God Almighty in it; for your heedlessness of the existence of your dhikr is more severe than your heedlessness with the existence of your dhikr. And perhaps He will raise you from dhikr with heedlessness to dhikr with vigilance, and from dhikr with vigilance to dhikr with presence, and from dhikr with presence to dhikr with absence from other than the Remembered. And that is not difficult for God.' (1)

And the types of verbal dhikr are many; among them: glorification (tasbīḥ), magnification (takbīr), recitation of the Qur'an, and other than that. And the swiftest of them in response for the beginner is 'there is no god but God' (lā ilāha illā Allāh) separate from 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God' (Muḥammadun Rasūl Allāh) according to verification, except for the conclusion (khatm). So if he intends the conclusion, he concludes with it. And in some of the Shādhilī ways, he mentions it at the head of every hundred. This is when he makes dhikr alone. But when he makes dhikr with a group, he only mentions it at the conclusion with his brethren. Hence the masters of the Muḥammadan ways proceeded to restrict themselves to it. So when the wayfarer (sālik) becomes complete, it is best for him to combine with it 'Muḥammad is the Messenger of God'. And the best then is to occupy himself with recitation of the Qur'an to be characterized by it and for the esoteric sciences (al-ʿulūm al-laduniyya) to be poured upon him from its secrets. And if he does not memorize the Qur'an, he should occupy himself with listening to it from whoever recites it, even if the reciter is heedless. And the matter is like the saying of the knower of God, my master ʿUmar ibn al-Fāriḍ, may God [bless him]? (1).
Source pages p. 475

Definition and Stages of Spiritual Vigilance (Murāqaba)
Al-Sawi defines murāqaba and outlines its ascent to mushāhada and muʿāyana.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of spiritual vigilance (murāqaba), how it leads to witnessing (mushāhada) and direct sight (muʿāyana), and the experiential nature of these states.

Core Idea
Spiritual vigilance is active, constant awareness of God that transforms every moment into a path of witnessing.

In this passage, al-Sawi explains that murāqaba is not merely fear but an active, all-encompassing observation of God in every state. He illustrates with two vivid examples: resisting sin and recognizing God's sole agency in eating. The ultimate goal is to ascend from vigilance to witnessing (mushāhada) and then to direct sight (muʿāyana), which are mystical experiences beyond intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Notice the flow from definition to examples to higher stages.
The passage includes marginal commentary (qawlu) that clarifies points.
2
Understand the definition of murāqaba
Murāqaba is defined as constant observation of God. The examples of sin and eating show how this vigilance reveals God's presence and agency.
In the sin example, vigilance leads to desistance out of shame. In the eating example, it leads to recognizing God as the sole agent.
3
Trace the three stages
Identify the three stages: murāqaba (vigilance) → mushāhada (witnessing) → muʿāyana (direct sight). Note that mushāhada occurs when one realizes waḥdat al-afʿāl (oneness of acts), and muʿāyana occurs when one becomes absorbed in God.
The commentator suggests a nuanced terminology shift: 'witness' may be premature before full absorption.
4
Reflect on the commentary
The marginal notes clarify that 'states' (aḥwāl) is all-encompassing, and point out a possible misapplication of terms. Consider why the commentator might suggest 'vigilant' instead of 'witness'.
This shows the precision of spiritual terminology.
5
Conclude with the nature of these states
The passage ends by stating that these are dhawqiyya (experiential) matters beyond intellect, known only to purified souls. Reflect on what this means for the path of spiritual realization.
This reminds us that rational understanding alone is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المراقبة
مراقباً لله في الأحوال أي في جميع أحوالك، فإنَّك بالمراقبة : ترتقي إلى المشاهدة، وبالمشاهدة ترتقي إلى المعاينة.
والمراقبة: ملاحظة الحقِّ تعالى عند كلّ شيء، مثلاً إذا لاحظته حال قصد النَّفس الوقوع في المعصية وجدته تعالى مطلعاً عليك، فترجع عنها حياء منه، وإذا لاحظته حالَ أكلك وجدته تعالى هو الذي ساق إليك ذلك الطَّعامَ من غير حول منك ولا قوة لك، ثم وجدته حرَّك يدك إلى تناوله، وجعل فيك القدرة على رفعه لفمك، ثمَّ حرَّك فمك وأجرى فيه الرِّيق، ثمَّ خلق فيك قوَّة اللَّذَّة فساقه إلى المعدة، ثمَّ رتَّب على ذلك قوَّة في جسمك وربَّاك، فجعل منه للحم نصيباً وللعظم نصيباً وللعصب نصيباً، وما فضل ممَّا لا منفعة فيه أخرجه، فتعلم بذلك أنَّه لا فاعل سواه، فإذا قوي هذا المعنى فيك سُمِّي وحدة الأفعال، وصِرْتَ مشاهداً الله في كل شيء .
قوله: (أي: في جميع أشار بذلك إلى (أل) في الأحوال للاستغراق .
قوله : (وصرت مشاهداً ) : المناسب أن يقول : مراقباً .
وقوله : (فإذا قويت هذه المشاهدة المناسب : المراقبة .
فإذا قويت هذه المشاهدة حتَّى غِبتَ عمَّا سوى الله سُمِّيت معاينة الذات، فإذا زاد التّمكين شاهدت بعد ذلك أنه خالق لعبده وما عمل، وهذا معنى قولهم: مشاهدة الله قبل كل شيء)، وهذه أمور ذوقية من وراء طور العقل، لا يعرفها إلّا أهلُ العنايات والنُّفوس القدسية وعنا بهم .
Vigilance. Be vigilant for God in states, i.e. in all your states, for by vigilance you ascend to witnessing, and by witnessing you ascend to direct sight. And vigilance is observation of the truth Most High in every thing. For example, if you observe Him when the soul intends to fall into sin, you find Him Most High aware of you, so you desist out of shame from Him. And if you observe Him when you eat, you find Him Most High is the One who brought you that food without any power or strength from you, then you find Him moved your hand to take it, and placed in you the ability to raise it to your mouth, then He moved your mouth and flowed saliva in it, then He created in you the power of pleasure and directed it to the stomach, then He arranged thereby strength in your body and nurtured you, and made of it a share for flesh, a share for bone, and a share for nerve; and what remains that has no benefit, He expels. So you learn thereby that there is no agent other than Him. When this meaning becomes strong in you, it is called the unity of acts, and you become a witness of God in everything. His statement: (i.e. in all) he indicated by that that the alif-lam in 'states' is for encompassment. His statement: (And you become a witness) the appropriate thing is that he say: vigilant. And his statement: (When this witnessing becomes strong) the appropriate is: vigilance. When this witnessing becomes strong until you become absent from all besides God, it is called direct sight of the essence. When empowerment increases, you then witness that He is the creator of His servant and what he does. This is the meaning of their statement: 'Witnessing God before everything.' These are mystical matters beyond the realm of intellect, known only to the people of divine care and purified souls, and God cares for them.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the concept of spiritual vigilance (murāqaba) and its progression to higher states of divine witnessing. The main text begins by stating that vigilance raises one to witnessing (mushāhada) and then to direct sight (muʿāyana). It then defines vigilance as the constant observation of God in all circumstances, providing concrete examples: when one intends sin, vigilance makes one aware of God's awareness, leading to desistance out of shame; when eating, vigilance reveals God as the sole provider and agent, moving the limbs and coordinating digestion, leading to the realization that there is no agent but God. This understanding, when deeply rooted, is called the oneness of acts (waḥdat al-afʿāl), and the person becomes a witness of God in everything. The marginal commentary (qawlu) clarifies that 'states' encompasses all states, and notes a terminological nuance: the text says 'you become a witness' but the commentator suggests 'vigilant' would be more appropriate in that stage, and similarly for the next stage. The main text then continues: further strengthening leads to a state of complete absorption (ghayba) in God, called muʿāyana of the essence, where one witnesses that God is the creator of all actions. This is explained as 'witnessing God before everything'. The author concludes that these are experiential realities (dhawqiyya) beyond the capacity of rational intellect, known only to those endowed with divine care and purified souls.

Key Terms
مراقبة
مشاهدة
معاينة
وحدة الأفعال
ذوقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think murāqaba is just fear or passive caution.
Correction: Murāqaba is active, constant observation of God in all states, leading to deeper spiritual insights and transformation.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does murāqaba (vigilance) lead to?
A) Fear of God
B) Mushāhada (witnessing) then Muʿāyana (direct sight)
C) Good deeds only
D) Knowledge of Islamic law

Key Takeaway
Murāqaba is the first step of a spiritual journey that, when deepened, reveals God's sole agency and leads to direct experiential knowledge of Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage describes how vigilance makes you desist from sin out of shame of God's awareness. When was the last time you stopped yourself from a wrong action because you felt God's presence? What practical step can you take today to strengthen that feeling?
?
When you eat your next meal, will you deliberately pause and reflect on the fact that God moved your hand and provided the food? How would that change your gratitude and your awareness of His constant involvement in your life?
?
These spiritual states are said to be beyond intellect, requiring purification. Are you willing to pursue this path of purification, even if it demands effort and discipline? What one change in your daily routine could bring you closer to constant vigilance?

The Murid's Etiquette: Humility and Self-Critique
Al-Sawi enumerates seven etiquettes for the murid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key etiquettes (adab) that a spiritual seeker should cultivate, including thinking ill of oneself, abandoning revenge, seeing one's worship as deficient, not speaking of advanced states prematurely, and praying for enemies and sinful believers.

Core Idea
True spiritual progress begins with humility and self-accounting.

In this passage, Al-Sawi continues his list of essential etiquettes for the murid (disciple). These practices cultivate humility, sincerity, and detachment from ego. They also set the stage for understanding the inner thoughts that can affect one's spiritual state.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of etiquettes
Read items 6-9 and 11-13 from the Arabic and translation. Notice the practical instructions.
Each item begins with 'ومنها' (and among them).
2
Reflect on the underlying principle
Observe that each etiquette involves turning away from self-importance and toward others, including enemies.
Item 6: think ill of yourself and well of others.
3
Connect to self-accounting
Consider how these adab prepare the heart for the purification of thoughts, which is discussed next.
Muhasabat al-nafs is introduced in item 10.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦ - ومنها : سوء الظَّنِّ بنفسه وحسنه بغيره، حتّى يرى أنَّ كلَّ أحد أحسن منه حالاً .
٧ - ومنها : ألا ينتصر لنفسه في أمر .
٨ - ومنها : أن يرى عبادته دائماً قد دخلها الخللُ مِنَ الرِّياء والخواطر الرَّديَّة، ومثلُها يستحقُ عليها العقاب لولا مسامحة الله تعالى له فيستغفر من عبادته ومن استغفاره.
٩ - ومنها : ألا يتكلم بكلام العارفين من الفرق والجمع، والبقاء والفناء ما لم يكمل، على أنَّ الأولى للكامل ترك ذلك إلا لحاجة تقتضي ذلك .
١٠ - ومنها: محاسبةُ النَّفس على ما ارتكبته من المحرمات والمكروهات وفضولِ المباحاتِ، وعلى ما وقع في نفسه من الخواطر النَّفسانيةِ والشَّيطانية والاستغفار منها .
والفرقُ بين الخاطرِ النَّفساني والشَّيطاني:
- أنَّ الأول : يكون بإلحاح على المعصية أو الشهوة؛ كالطفل الذي يلح على أمه حتّى تعطيه ما يريد، فيجب قمعها عن ذلك بملازمة الذكر وبيان عاقبة هذا الأمر والتوجه إلى الشيخ.
قوله : (إلا لحاجة تقتضي ذلك) : أي : كالتعليم.
قوله: (والفرق بين خاطر النفساني ... إلخ): الذي ذكره غيره أنَّ
- والثاني : يكون من غير إلحاح، بل يأمر بالمعصية ويزينها، فإن طاوعه الشَّخص وإلَّا انتقل لآخر ؛ لأنَّ قَصْدَه الغواية على أي حالة تكون لا معصية بخصوصها .
وأما الفرق بين الخاطرِ الرَّباني والخاطر الملكي
- أنَّ الأول : ما فيه تنبيه على الخير من غير حثٌ، ولا يؤدي إلى حيرة .
—
- والثاني : ما فيه حثّ على الطاعة.
١١ - ومنها : مدحُ أعدائه، وعدم التكدر من ذكرهم، والدُّعاء لهم بالمغفرة والتوفيق ١٢ - ومنها : الدُّعاء لعصاة المؤمنين كذلك.
١٣ - ومنها : مطالعة كتب القوم ليتعلّم منها الأدب، ويعرف منها حال أهل الله تعالى، فبالآداب ترتقي إلى مقام الأحباب، أنشدنا شيخنا :
الخاطر النَّفساني : ما يلزم معصية بعينها، والشَّيطاني: ما يلزم معصية لا بعينها، والرَّحماني: ما يلزم طاعة بعينها، والملكي : ما يلزم طاعة لا بعينها .
قوله : (ومنها : مدح أعدائه) : فيجاهد نفسه على ذلك حتّى يتخلق به،
كما قال بعض العارفين (١) :
(١) البيت لشهاب الدين السهروردي في ديوانه» (ص (٦٢).
6. And among them: thinking ill of oneself and well of others, until he sees that everyone is better than him in condition. 7. And among them: not taking revenge for himself in any matter. 8. And among them: always seeing his worship as having entered deficiency from hypocrisy (riya') and bad thoughts (khawatir radiyya), and that such deeds deserve punishment were it not for God's forbearance, so he seeks forgiveness from his worship and from his seeking forgiveness. 9. And among them: not speaking the speech of the knowers (al-‘arifin) about separation (al-farq) and union (al-jam‘), subsistence (al-baqa') and annihilation (al-fana') until he is complete, although it is preferable for the complete one to leave that except for a need that necessitates it. 10. And among them: self-accounting (muhasabat al-nafs) for what it has committed of prohibitions, disliked things, and excess of permissible things, and for what has occurred in his self of psychological (nafsani) and satanic (shaytani) thoughts, and seeking forgiveness from them. The difference between the psychological thought (al-khatir al-nafsani) and the satanic thought (al-khatir al-shaytani): - The first: it is insistent upon sin or desire, like a child who insists on his mother until she gives him what he wants, so it is necessary to suppress it by constant remembrance (dhikr), clarifying the consequence of this matter, and turning to the shaykh. His saying: (except for a need that necessitates it): i.e., like teaching. His saying: (The difference between the nafsani thought... etc.): What others mentioned is that - The second: it is without insistence, rather it commands sin and beautifies it; if the person obeys it, fine, otherwise it moves to another, because its aim is misguidance in any state, not a particular sin. As for the difference between the lordly thought (al-khatir al-rabbani) and the angelic thought (al-khatir al-malaki): - The first: it contains a reminder of good without urging, and does not lead to confusion. - The second: it contains urging to obedience. 11. And among them: praising his enemies, not being distressed by mentioning them, and supplicating for them with forgiveness and success. 12. And among them: supplicating for sinful believers likewise. 13. And among them: studying the books of the people (the Sufis) to learn from them etiquette (adab) and to know from them the state of the people of God, for by the etiquettes one ascends to the station of the beloved ones. Our shaykh recited to us: The psychological thought: what necessitates a particular sin, and the satanic: what necessitates sin not particular, and the lordly: what necessitates a particular obedience, and the angelic: what necessitates obedience not particular. His saying: (Among them: praising his enemies): he struggles against his soul until he is characterized by that, as one of the knowers said: (1) The line is by Shihab al-Din al-Suhrawardi in his Diwan, p. 62. [From al-Kamil meter]
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a combination of an enumeration and a definition. It continues a list of etiquettes (adab) for the murid (disciple) and includes a precise taxonomy of inner thoughts (khawatir). The text first lists items 6-10, which are practical instructions: thinking ill of oneself (item 6), not taking revenge (7), seeing one's worship as deficient (8), not speaking about advanced spiritual states prematurely (9), and self-accounting for sins and thoughts (10). At item 10, the author introduces the distinction between the psychological (nafsani) and satanic (shaytani) thought. The nafsani thought is characterized by insistence on a particular sin or desire, like a child insisting on his mother, and requires suppression through dhikr, understanding consequences, and seeking the shaykh. The shaytani thought is not insistent; it merely commands sin and beautifies it, and if rejected, moves to another sin because its goal is misguidance in general. The author then gives the difference between the lordly (rabbani) and angelic (malaki) thoughts: the rabbani inspires goodness without urging and does not cause confusion, while the malaki urges to obedience. After the definitions, items 11-13 continue the list: praising enemies, supplicating for sinful believers, and studying Sufi books to learn adab. The passage concludes with a summary verse (likely a poem) that succinctly defines all four types: nafsani necessitates a particular sin, shaytani necessitates sin in general, rahmani (variant of rabbani) necessitates a particular obedience, and malaki necessitates obedience in general. The commentary (qawlahu) clarifies that the item about praising enemies involves struggling against one's soul until that becomes a character trait.

Key Terms
خاطر (khatir)
محاسبة النفس (muhasabat al-nafs)
رِياء (riya')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what should a murid think of others?
A) They are worse than him
B) They are better than him
C) They are equal to him
D) It depends on the situation

Key Takeaway
The foundation of spiritual growth is humility, self-critique, and sincere concern for others, including enemies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these seven etiquettes stings you the most to read? That sting is your nafs resisting its medicine. What one concrete step will you take today to practice that specific etiquette?
?
You have likely felt wronged by someone. The passage forbids taking revenge (item 7). Is there a person you have not forgiven in your heart? Will you pray for them tonight, as item 11 commands?
?
Item 6 says: 'Think ill of your own state and consider others better.' When you look at your prayer, do you secretly feel satisfied? Or do you see it as defective and beg Allah to accept it? Which attitude truly pleases Allah?

Distinguishing the Four Types of Spiritual Thoughts
Al-Sawi defines four types of khawatir and gives their distinguishing features.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the psychological (nafsani), satanic (shaytani), lordly (rabbani), and angelic (malaki) thoughts, based on their characteristics.

Core Idea
Not all inner thoughts are the same; each type has a distinct source and purpose.

Having established the basic etiquettes of the murid, Al-Sawi now delves into the inner world of thoughts (khawatir). The seeker must learn to identify the different types of thoughts that arise in his heart, as each requires a different response. This passage provides a precise classification.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of self-accounting
Read the opening of item 10 about muhasabat al-nafs. This is the practice that makes the classification necessary.
Muhasaba involves examining thoughts and seeking forgiveness.
2
Compare nafsani and shaytani thoughts
Note the key difference: nafsani is insistent on a specific sin; shaytani is not insistent and moves to another sin if rejected.
Nafsani is like a child insisting; shaytani beautifies sin.
3
Compare rabbani and malaki thoughts
Note that rabbani reminds of good without urging, while malaki urges to obedience.
Rabbani does not lead to confusion; malaki gives a push.
4
Memorize the summary verse
The poem succinctly captures all four types: nafsani (specific sin), shaytani (any sin), rahmani (specific obedience), malaki (any obedience).
The verse is attributed to Shihab al-Din al-Suhrawardi.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the nafsani and shaytani khawatir are the same.
Correction: The text distinguishes them by insistence: nafsani is insistent on a particular sin, while shaytani is not insistent and moves to another sin if rejected.

What distinguishes the shaytani (satanic) thought from the nafsani (psychological) thought according to this passage?
A) The shaytani thought is insistent on a specific sin.
B) The shaytani thought is not insistent and moves to another sin if rejected.
C) The shaytani thought always leads to confusion.
D) The shaytani thought is always accompanied by an urge to obedience.

Key Takeaway
The four types of khawatir (nafsani, shaytani, rabbani, malaki) are distinguished by whether they are insistent and whether they target a specific sin or obedience.

?

?

?
Think of a recent time you followed a bad thought. Could you classify it as nafsani or shaytani? How would identifying its type have helped you resist it more effectively?

Transformation Through Mujahada: Acquiring Muhammadan Character
The author describes the results of mujahada and the acquisition of Muhammadan character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how mujahada transforms the self and leads to acquiring Muhammadan character and the station of Allah's vicegerent.

Core Idea
Mujahada transforms blameworthy traits into praiseworthy ones, culminating in becoming Allah's vicegerent.

Mujahada is not merely a negative struggle; it yields positive fruits. The author explains the process by which the self is purified and adorned with the noble character of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This transformation elevates the believer to the rank of vicegerent on earth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transformation
Read the Arabic passage describing the results of mujahada carefully. Then read its translation.
Notice the conditional structure: 'fa-idha jahadta...' indicating cause and effect.
2
Identify the blameworthy traits replaced
The passage says blameworthy attributes are replaced by praiseworthy ones. Reflect on what 'blameworthy' might mean in this context.
3
List the bestowed Muhammadan traits
The passage enumerates specific traits: forbearance, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and others. Make a mental note of each.
These are not exhaustive but exemplify the noble character.
4
Reflect on vicegerency
Consider what it means to be 'Allah's vicegerent on earth.' How does this connect to the transformation described?
This is the ultimate station for the purified servant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا جاهدت النفس بما مرهان عليها - إن شاء الله تعالى - الخلوص من ظلمة الأغيار، وتبدلت صفاتها المذمومة بالصفات الممدوحة، فيخلع الحق تبارك وتعالى عليك خلع الأخلاق المحمدية من الحلم والعلم، والشفقة والرأفة والخضوع، والزهد والورع والسخاء، وغير ذلك من مكارم الأخلاق، كما أشرت إلى ذلك بقولي: لترتقي معالم الكمال أي: إلى معالم هي الأخلاق المحمدية، وحينئذ يكون هذا العبد خليفة الله في أرضه. وعلامة زوال الرعونات البشرية من القلب، والتحلي بالأخلاق المرضية: أن يستوي عنده المدح والذم، والمنع والإعطاء، وإقبال الناس عليه وإدبارهم، بل يرجح الذم والمنع والإدبار على مقابلها.
So when you struggle against the self with what it has been trained upon—if Allah wills—you will be delivered from the darkness of others, and its blameworthy attributes will be transformed into praiseworthy attributes. Then the Truth, Blessed and Exalted, will bestow upon you the garments of Muhammadan character: forbearance, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and other noble traits of character, as I alluded to in my saying: 'that you may ascend to the landmarks of perfection'—that is, to landmarks which are the Muhammadan character. At that time this servant becomes the vicegerent of Allah on His earth. And the sign of the removal of human pretensions from the heart and the adornment with pleasing character is that praise and blame, denial and giving, people's turning towards him and away from him become equal in his sight. Rather, he prefers blame, denial, and turning away over their opposites.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage discusses the transformative effects of spiritual struggle (mujahada). The author explains that when one struggles against the lower self according to the prescribed path (possibly the teachings of the spiritual master), with divine will, the self is purified from the darkness of other-than-God (al-aghyar). Its blameworthy qualities are replaced by praiseworthy ones, and Allah clothes the person with the Muhammadan character traits (akhlaq muhammadiyya) such as forbearance, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and others. This is the meaning of ascending to the landmarks of perfection. The person then becomes the vicegerent of Allah on earth. A key sign of this purification is that the person becomes indifferent to praise or blame, receiving or withholding, people's acceptance or rejection; they even prefer blame, denial, and rejection over their opposites, indicating complete detachment from ego and concern for others' opinions.

Key Terms
مجاهدة
الأخلاق المحمدية
خليفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Allah bestow upon the one who struggles against the self?
A) Wealth and status
B) Muhammadan character (akhlaq muhammadiyya)
C) Supernatural powers
D) Long life

Key Takeaway
Mujahada leads to the acquisition of Muhammadan character and the station of Allah's vicegerent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever truly struggled against your own blameworthy traits—like pride or stinginess—not as a casual effort, but as a relentless mujahada? If not, what is holding you back from starting today, and can you name one specific trait you will begin to fight this week?
?
The passage says that Allah bestows Muhammadan character upon you as a garment. Do you live as though you are clothed in these traits, or are you still wearing the rags of your old habits? What is one trait from the list (forbearance, mercy, humility, etc.) that you lack the most, and what concrete step will you take to acquire it through struggle?
?
If the ultimate result of mujahada is becoming Allah's vicegerent on Earth, do you believe your current state reflects that station? Where is the gap between what you claim to be and what you actually are, and will you commit to praying for divine help to close it?

The Sign of Spiritual Purification: Equanimity Towards Praise and Blame
The author identifies the sign of removal of human pretensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sign of spiritual purification as the equality of praise and blame in one's heart, and the preference for blame.

Core Idea
The sign of true purification is complete equanimity towards praise, blame, giving, and withholding.

The author not only describes the results of mujahada but also provides a clear sign for recognizing genuine purification. This sign involves detachment from people's opinions and reactions, even preferring blame and denial over their opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the sign
Carefully read the Arabic passage that defines the sign of purification, then its translation.
Note the key phrase: 'wa 'alāmatu zawāli ar-ru'ūnāt...'
2
Understand the concept of equanimity
The sign is that praise and blame, giving and withholding, people's turning towards and away become equal in one's sight. Reflect on how difficult this is.
3
Analyze the preference for blame
The passage adds that the purified person even prefers blame, denial, and turning away. Why would that be? Consider the danger of attachment to praise.
This indicates complete detachment from ego.
4
Apply to daily life
Think of personal experiences where you were affected by praise or blame. How can you work towards this equanimity?
This is a practical spiritual goal.

So when you struggle against the self with what it has been trained upon—if Allah wills—you will be delivered from the darkness of others, and its blameworthy attributes will be transformed into praiseworthy attributes. Then the Truth, Blessed and Exalted, will bestow upon you the garments of Muhammadan character: forbearance, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and other noble traits of character, as I alluded to in my saying: 'that you may ascend to the landmarks of perfection'—that is, to landmarks which are the Muhammadan character. At that time this servant becomes the vicegerent of Allah on His earth. And the sign of the removal of human pretensions from the heart and the adornment with pleasing character is that praise and blame, denial and giving, people's turning towards him and away from him become equal in his sight. Rather, he prefers blame, denial, and turning away over their opposites.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage discusses the transformative effects of spiritual struggle (mujahada). The author explains that when one struggles against the lower self according to the prescribed path (possibly the teachings of the spiritual master), with divine will, the self is purified from the darkness of other-than-God (al-aghyar). Its blameworthy qualities are replaced by praiseworthy ones, and Allah clothes the person with the Muhammadan character traits (akhlaq muhammadiyya) such as forbearance, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and others. This is the meaning of ascending to the landmarks of perfection. The person then becomes the vicegerent of Allah on earth. A key sign of this purification is that the person becomes indifferent to praise or blame, receiving or withholding, people's acceptance or rejection; they even prefer blame, denial, and rejection over their opposites, indicating complete detachment from ego and concern for others' opinions.

Correction: Equanimity here means not being attached to people's praise or blame; it does not mean neglecting good deeds or moral responsibility.

?
This lesson says the sign of purification is that giving and withholding become equal. Is there a possession or opportunity you are holding onto tightly, afraid of losing? Honestly examine your attachment. Are you ready to accept Allah's decree if He withholds it from you? Make a sincere du'a to detach your heart from everything but Him.

The Fruit of Spiritual Struggle: Transformation of the Self
Al-Sawi describes the transformation through spiritual struggle and the attainment of prophetic character.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the fruit of sincere spiritual struggle is the transformation of blameworthy traits into praiseworthy ones and the attainment of Muhammadan character, making one a vicegerent of Allah.

Core Idea
Struggle against the self transforms blame into praise and clothes you in prophetic character.

Al-Sawi begins by quoting a verse on the value of intellect and discipline, then explains the process of spiritual struggle. He describes how God replaces blameworthy attributes with praiseworthy ones, ultimately clothing the seeker with the very character of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This passage lays out the direct result of sincere self-discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening verse and its explanation
The lesson opens with a poetic verse emphasizing that intellect and discipline are God's best gifts and constitute the life of a person.
Reflect on why discipline is paired with intellect.
2
Understand the process of struggling against the soul
Al-Sawi explains that when you struggle against the soul through discipline, you achieve deliverance from the darkness of others and your blameworthy attributes become praiseworthy.
This transformation is the direct fruit of jihad al-nafs.
3
Identify the Muhammadan character traits
The passage lists traits such as clemency, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, and generosity as the garments of prophetic character.
These are the qualities that God bestows on the seeker.
4
Recognize the ultimate goal
Al-Sawi states that the one adorned with these traits becomes God's vicegerent on earth.
This is a high station – a representative of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما وهب الله لامرئ هبه أحسن من عقله وأدبه هما حياة الفتى فإن عدما فإن فقد الحياة أجمل به

فإذا جاهدت النفس بما مرهان عليها - إن شاء الله تعالى - الخلوص من ظلمة الأغيار، وتبدلت صفاتها المذمومة بالصفات الممدوحة، فيخلع الحق تبارك وتعالى عليك خلع الأخلاق المحمدية من الحلم والعلم، والشفقة والرأفة والخضوع، والزهد والورع والسخاء، وغير ذلك من مكارم الأخلاق، كما أشرت إلى ذلك بقولي: لترتقي معالم الكمال أي: إلى معالم هي الأخلاق المحمدية، وحينئذ يكون هذا العبد خليفة الله في أرضه. وعلامة زوال الرعونات البشرية من القلب، والتحلي بالأخلاق المرضية: أن يستوي عنده المدح والذم، والمنع والإعطاء، وإقبال الناس عليه وإدبارهم، بل يرجح الذم والمنع والإدبار على مقابلها.

قوله: (بل يرجح الذم والمنع ... إلخ): قال صاحب الحكمة في هذا المعنى: (ورود الفاقات أعياد المريدين)
What God has given to a man, His best gift is his intellect and his discipline; they are the life of the youth, and if they are lost, then loss of life is more beautiful. So when you struggle against the soul through the discipline imposed upon it—if God wills—[you will achieve] deliverance from the darkness of others, and its blameworthy attributes will be transformed into praiseworthy attributes. Then the Truth, Blessed and Exalted, will clothe you with the garments of Muhammadan character: clemency, knowledge, compassion, mercy, humility, asceticism, piety, generosity, and other noble traits of character, as I alluded to in my saying: 'That you may ascend to the landmarks of perfection'—meaning to the landmarks which are the Muhammadan characters. Then this servant becomes the vicegerent of God on His earth. And the sign of the removal of human frivolities from the heart and the adornment with pleasing character is that praise and blame, denial and giving, people's turning toward him and turning away from him become equal in his view; rather, he gives preference to blame, denial, and turning away over their opposites. [The perfections, and they are] Imitate, if you are not like them; for imitation of (noble) men is success. His saying: 'Rather, he gives preference to blame and denial ... etc.': The author of al-Ḥikam said concerning this meaning: 'The arrival of needs are the feast of the seekers.'
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line of poetry and elaborates on the fruits of spiritual struggle (jihad al-nafs). The author begins by quoting a verse: the best gifts God gives are intellect and discipline, which constitute the life of a person. Then he explains that when one struggles against the soul with proper discipline, God willing, the soul is purified from the darkness of otherness (al-aghyar) and blameworthy traits are replaced with praiseworthy ones. God then clothes the seeker with the prophetic character traits (al-akhlaq al-Muhammadiyya), such as clemency, knowledge, compassion, humility, asceticism, and generosity. At this stage, the servant becomes God's vicegerent on earth. The sign of this transformation is complete equanimity: praise and blame, giving and withholding, people's acceptance or rejection all become equal to him; in fact, he prefers blame and deprivation over their opposites, because this indicates detachment from ego. The author then inserts a line of poetry encouraging emulation of the perfect, and cites a maxim from Ibn 'Ata'illah's al-Ḥikam: 'The arrival of needs are the feast of the seekers'—meaning that trials and needs are occasions for drawing closer to God. The overall teaching is that true spiritual maturity is measured not by external approval but by inner detachment and preference for humility.

الأخلاق المحمدية

The Sign of Prophetic Character: Equanimity in Praise and Blame
Al-Sawi presents the sign of attaining prophetic character: equanimity towards praise and blame, with preference for hardship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the ultimate sign of spiritual maturity is complete equanimity towards praise and blame, even preferring what is difficult.

Core Idea
True spiritual maturity is measured by indifference to praise and preference for blame.

Having explained the transformation, Al-Sawi now gives the definitive sign that one has truly attained prophetic character: that praise and blame become equal, and one even prefers blame and hardship. He supports this with a profound maxim from Ibn 'Ata'illah. This passage helps us test our own spiritual state.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of the sign
Al-Sawi states that the sign of having removed human frivolities is that praise and blame, giving and denying, people's turning toward and away become equal.
This is a state of inner detachment from external approval.
2

The passage adds that the truly advanced person actually prefers blame, denial, and turning away over their opposites.
This shows a deep preference for humility and hardship.
3
Reflect on the poem about imitation
The inserted verse encourages emulating the perfect, indicating that one should strive to reach this state.
Imitation of the noble leads to success.
4
Consider the supporting maxim
Al-Sawi quotes Ibn 'Ata'illah: 'The arrival of needs are the feast of the seekers' – trials are occasions for spiritual growth.
This reinforces the idea that difficulties are gifts.

The Supplication of the Broken-Hearted and the Call for Humility
Al-Sawi presents a supplication for protection from worldly distractions and emphasizes the state of broken-heartedness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the supplication taught by Imam al-Sawi for protection from worldly distractions and the spiritual state of brokenness that it requires.

Core Idea
God is with the broken-hearted—humility is the key to His presence.

Imam al-Sawi presents a powerful supplication that the seeker should utter with complete humility. This lesson focuses on the du'a itself and the underlying spiritual condition of brokenness that invites God's presence. Let us explore the meaning of this sacred plea.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication in Arabic
Read the Arabic text of the du'a carefully. Notice its wording: 'O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter from every trial.'
The supplication is short but profound.
2
Understand the state of brokenness
Al-Sawi explains that the supplication should be uttered with lowliness (dhull) and that God is with those whose hearts are broken. Reflect on how humility and brokenness are prerequisites for divine nearness.
He cites a sacred hadith: 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.'
3
Identify what the supplication seeks
The du'a asks not to be cut off from God by any 'cutter' (qāṭiʿ) that distracts the heart from worship. The 'cutters' include love of wealth, children, status, and desires.
These are explained further in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دعاء

(وقل) متضرعاً إلى ربك قولاً ملتبساً بالذل، فإن الله تعالى عند المنكسرة قلوبهم: يا رب لا تقطعني عنك بقاطع من كل فتنة يشتغل القلب بها عن العبودية، من حب المال والولد والجاه والشهوات إنما أموالكم وأولادكم فتنة، زين للناس حب الشهوات من النساء والبنين... الآية، يأيها الذين آمنوا لا تلهكم أموالكم ولا أولادكم عن ذكر الله ومن يفعل ذلك فأولئك هم الخسرون.

قوله: (بذل): جعله الشارح متعلقاً بمحذوف صفة لمصدر محذوف مفعول مطلق لـ (قل)، والباء للملابسة وفيه كلفة والأسهل جعل الجار متعلقاً بمحذوف حالاً من فاعل (قل)، والتقدير: قل: يا رب لا تقطعني ... إلخ، حال كونك ملتبساً بالذل.

والمجرور

قوله: (فإن الله تعالى عند المنكسرة قلوبهم): تعليل لما قبله، وفيه اقتباس من الحديث القدسي: «أنا عند المنكسرة قلوبهم من أجلي»

قوله: (من كل فتنة): بيان للقاطع.

وقوله: (من) حب المال ... إلخ) بيان للفتنة.

قوله: (إنما أموالكم وأولادكم فتنة ... إلخ): هذه أدلة ثلاثة على ما ذكره من أن حب المال والولد والشهوات من جملة القواطع.
Supplication. (And say), humbly imploring your Lord, a saying clothed in lowliness, for indeed God Almighty is with those whose hearts are broken: 'O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter from every trial that occupies the heart with it from worship, from the love of wealth, children, status, and desires. [Qur'an: ] Your wealth and your children are only a trial. [Qur'an: ] Adorned for people is the love of desires from women and children... the verse. [Qur'an: ] O you who believe, let not your wealth and your children divert you from the remembrance of God; and whoever does that, they are the losers.' His saying: 'with lowliness' ('bādhal'): The commentator made it attached to an omitted [word] as an attribute of an omitted verbal noun which is the direct object of 'say' (qul), and the 'ba' for accompaniment, but there is difficulty in that; the easier [analysis] is to make the prepositional phrase attached to an omitted [word] as a circumstantial clause from the subject of 'say', and the estimation is: Say: O Lord, do not cut me off... etc., while you are clothed in lowliness. And the ma'rūd? His saying: 'For indeed God Almighty is with those whose hearts are broken': this is a reason for what precedes, and it contains a borrowing from the sacred hadith: 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.' His saying: 'from every trial': it is an explanation of the cutter. And his saying: 'from the love of wealth... etc.' is an explanation of the trial. His saying: 'Your wealth and your children are only a trial... etc.': these are three proofs for what he mentioned, that the love of wealth, children, and desires is among the cutters.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage presents a supplication (du'a) that the seeker should utter, clothed in humility and lowliness. The supplication asks God not to cut the servant off from Him by any 'cutter' (qāṭi')—meaning anything that distracts the heart from worship. The 'cutters' are specified as love of wealth, children, status, and desires. The author then provides grammatical analysis of the word 'bādhil' (meaning clothed in lowliness), noting two possible syntactic constructions. He then explains the clause 'for indeed God is with those whose hearts are broken' as a justification for the supplication, and cites a sacred hadith (al-ḥadīth al-qudsī) that God says 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.' The phrase 'from every trial' (min kull fitna) is an explanation of the 'cutter' (qāṭi'), and 'from the love of wealth...' specifies the nature of the trial. Finally, the author cites three Quranic verses (64:15, 3:14, 63:9) as evidence that these worldly attachments are indeed trials and distractions from God. The lesson emphasizes that the state of brokenness (‘taking recourse to God with a lowly heart’) is the condition that draws God's presence, and that genuine spiritual progress requires vigilance against the temptations of worldly attractions.

Key Terms
المنكسرة قلوبهم
الذل
الدعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the supplication asks for removal of all trials and difficulties.
Correction: The supplication specifically asks not to be cut off from God by trials, meaning that trials themselves can be beneficial if they do not distract from God. It is about maintaining connection despite trials, not avoiding them entirely.

Checkpoint

A) With anger
B) With humility and lowliness
C) With confidence and pride
D) With doubt

Key Takeaway
Humility and brokenness before God are the conditions for His nearness, and the supplication seeks protection from being cut off by worldly distractions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Name one 'cutter'—love of wealth, children, status, or desires—that has most recently pulled your heart away from Allah. Will you today beg Him to protect you from it, with tears of humility?
?
If God is with the broken-hearted, why do you so often try to appear strong and self-sufficient before Him? What would change in your life if you let yourself be truly broken in front of Him tonight?

Understanding the Cutters: Grammatical Analysis and Quranic Proofs
Al-Sawi provides grammatical analysis and Quranic proofs for the supplication's meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical structure of the phrase 'with lowliness' (bādhal) and the Quranic evidence that worldly attachments are trials that can cut one off from God.

Core Idea
Worldly attachments are 'cutters' that distract from worship, confirmed by Quranic verses.

In the previous lesson, we learned the supplication and its emphasis on humility. Now, Imam al-Sawi provides a grammatical analysis of the word 'bādhal' (with lowliness) and cites three Quranic verses proving that love of wealth, children, and desires are indeed trials that can cut one off from God. Let us delve into this explanatory portion.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the grammar of 'bādhal'
Al-Sawi discusses two possible syntactic analyses of 'bādhal' (with lowliness). Read the explanation and try to understand both interpretations.
The first analysis sees it as an attribute of an omitted verbal noun; the second as a circumstantial clause.
2
Understand the 'cutter' and 'trial'
Al-Sawi says 'from every trial' (min kull fitna) explains the 'cutter', and 'from the love of wealth...' explains the 'trial'. Grasp this layered explanation.
The 'cutter' is the trial itself; the specific trials are those attachments.
3
Reflect on the three Quranic verses
Al-Sawi cites three verses: 'Your wealth and children are only a trial' (64:15), 'Adorned for people is the love of desires...' (3:14), and 'Let not your wealth and children divert you...' (63:9). These prove that these attachments are indeed cutters.
Each verse emphasizes the distracting nature of worldly things.

دعاء

(وقل) متضرعاً إلى ربك قولاً ملتبساً بالذل، فإن الله تعالى عند المنكسرة قلوبهم: يا رب لا تقطعني عنك بقاطع من كل فتنة يشتغل القلب بها عن العبودية، من حب المال والولد والجاه والشهوات إنما أموالكم وأولادكم فتنة، زين للناس حب الشهوات من النساء والبنين... الآية، يأيها الذين آمنوا لا تلهكم أموالكم ولا أولادكم عن ذكر الله ومن يفعل ذلك فأولئك هم الخسرون.

قوله: (بذل): جعله الشارح متعلقاً بمحذوف صفة لمصدر محذوف مفعول مطلق لـ (قل)، والباء للملابسة وفيه كلفة والأسهل جعل الجار متعلقاً بمحذوف حالاً من فاعل (قل)، والتقدير: قل: يا رب لا تقطعني ... إلخ، حال كونك ملتبساً بالذل.

والمجرور

قوله: (فإن الله تعالى عند المنكسرة قلوبهم): تعليل لما قبله، وفيه اقتباس من الحديث القدسي: «أنا عند المنكسرة قلوبهم من أجلي»

قوله: (من كل فتنة): بيان للقاطع.

وقوله: (من) حب المال ... إلخ) بيان للفتنة.

قوله: (إنما أموالكم وأولادكم فتنة ... إلخ): هذه أدلة ثلاثة على ما ذكره من أن حب المال والولد والشهوات من جملة القواطع.
Supplication. (And say), humbly imploring your Lord, a saying clothed in lowliness, for indeed God Almighty is with those whose hearts are broken: 'O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter from every trial that occupies the heart with it from worship, from the love of wealth, children, status, and desires. [Qur'an: ] Your wealth and your children are only a trial. [Qur'an: ] Adorned for people is the love of desires from women and children... the verse. [Qur'an: ] O you who believe, let not your wealth and your children divert you from the remembrance of God; and whoever does that, they are the losers.' His saying: 'with lowliness' ('bādhal'): The commentator made it attached to an omitted [word] as an attribute of an omitted verbal noun which is the direct object of 'say' (qul), and the 'ba' for accompaniment, but there is difficulty in that; the easier [analysis] is to make the prepositional phrase attached to an omitted [word] as a circumstantial clause from the subject of 'say', and the estimation is: Say: O Lord, do not cut me off... etc., while you are clothed in lowliness. And the ma'rūd? His saying: 'For indeed God Almighty is with those whose hearts are broken': this is a reason for what precedes, and it contains a borrowing from the sacred hadith: 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.' His saying: 'from every trial': it is an explanation of the cutter. And his saying: 'from the love of wealth... etc.' is an explanation of the trial. His saying: 'Your wealth and your children are only a trial... etc.': these are three proofs for what he mentioned, that the love of wealth, children, and desires is among the cutters.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage presents a supplication (du'a) that the seeker should utter, clothed in humility and lowliness. The supplication asks God not to cut the servant off from Him by any 'cutter' (qāṭi')—meaning anything that distracts the heart from worship. The 'cutters' are specified as love of wealth, children, status, and desires. The author then provides grammatical analysis of the word 'bādhil' (meaning clothed in lowliness), noting two possible syntactic constructions. He then explains the clause 'for indeed God is with those whose hearts are broken' as a justification for the supplication, and cites a sacred hadith (al-ḥadīth al-qudsī) that God says 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.' The phrase 'from every trial' (min kull fitna) is an explanation of the 'cutter' (qāṭi'), and 'from the love of wealth...' specifies the nature of the trial. Finally, the author cites three Quranic verses (64:15, 3:14, 63:9) as evidence that these worldly attachments are indeed trials and distractions from God. The lesson emphasizes that the state of brokenness (‘taking recourse to God with a lowly heart’) is the condition that draws God's presence, and that genuine spiritual progress requires vigilance against the temptations of worldly attractions.

The Quran warns that wealth and children are a trial. In what specific way does your concern for them distract you from worship or remembrance of God? What concrete change will you make this week to ensure they draw you closer to Him instead?
